<Text>We ended up here when my Mediterranean place was last minute vetoed...

This used to be the old spot of East Borough- a modern Vietnamese place I used to go to when I lived nearby. They had great food and drinks- so when I discovered it was a familiar location I was a bit skeptical...

PEOPLE. The people were friendly, staff and managers rushed around attentively, and for a cozy place like this they had ample staff- no problems waiting around trying to flag down a server there. Only one minor incident when I was almost bashed by the kitchen door coming out of the restroom but otherwise very attentive staff.

FOOD. Menu had a bit of everything, it was like a Japanese diner that focused on sandwich and small bites and some ramen.
- takoyaki was a highlight, surprisingly pretty darn tasty, would definitely be something I‚Äôd order again
- salad was huuuuuge we got the full and it came in a salad bowl so if you‚Äôre ordering a salad get the half size
- sandwich hmmm the guild was interesting, don‚Äôt know if it was the horse radish or wasabi but it brought a little kick to the sandwich. The pork katsu was good too
- ramen: would skip these, unless you had no where else to go. (Sawtelle isn‚Äôt too far if you want more authentic ramen)
- dessert: this was interesting, I didn‚Äôt  particularly like this but my friends raved about it, they enjoyed the black sesame ice cream<//Text><Date>1564508020206</Date><Name>Babs Sheng<//Name><Rate>4< /Rate></record></dataset><record>

<rate>3<//rate><Review>It's official: I love the Kastu sando. This is simple comfort food, my friends--it's good because it's fried meat and a schmear on soft white bread. Nothing terribly complicated, just a well presented sandwich that, paired with a glass of wine feels like a little Monday night indulgence.

Happy hour runs from 3-6 pm daily--get the shishito peppers and a half priced cocktail! Also, be sure to check in on Yelp for a free chicken gyoza. We snuck in jusssssst past happy hour and didn't snag any of the deals, and I can't say this place feels particularly cheap in the food/drink department (about $10 for the sandwich and $13 for a glass of Summer Water ros√©, which is about the price of an entire bottle of that stuff). They also add a 15% service charge to your bill so we didn't tip on top of that. Would've appreciated a heads up/quick explanation on what that charge was so we didn't feel in the dark about it, but not a huge deal.

The biggest downside of this experience was the staff--they seemed super bummed out to be there and kind of like we were bothering them. Parking also isn't great in this part of Culver City! I usually park in the lot by Akasha but there is some metered parking out front if you want to take your chances on that. TL;DR? Come for happy hour, get yourself a sando, read your receipt thoroughly!<//Review>< pics>

< Text>
I'm giving this a 3.5 star.

Had the katsu sando, guild sando, wings, Kirin draft, and fat lip. The guild sando was pretty good.  Great flavor, bread was buttered.   I'd recommend it over the katsu sando.  The katsu sando wasn't bad.  I didn't find that it was dry.  It was made well, but nothing special about it.

Wings were okay.  Nothing to write about.  I wish they have 8 "wings" vs 6 and wish they were actual wings vs mini drumsticks.

Overall it was a good experience, nothing great, but I probably won't be back.  Kirin draft for $6 is great however for downtown Culver.

I wish they had something more substantive on their menu than sandwiches and ramen but being that it's a tavern, I guess I understand.  It's a bit too simple for me.

Nostalgic atmosphere with 90s hip hop music.

I also think the mandatory 15% tip is lame as I always double tax as my tip (19-20%).  But to make it mandatory and then leave another line for "additional tip", to me, is a slap in the face.</Text>

< review>
Really enjoyed this wing place. The environment is cool. It's brand new and has a modern design. The wings are really good. I tried the boneless and bone-in wings. Boneless wings are very unique compared to other chicken places. All of the wings tasted crispy and fresh. They put the perfect amount of sauce for me. It wasnt drenched in it, but it was just enough to get all of the flavor. I tried the California, hot, and lemon pepper wings. None of them we're very spicy. The only bad thing I have to say is that the French fries we're just alright. Tastes very similar to Jack in the box curly fries.

All in all it was one of my favorite wing places.
They have quite a bit of flavors to try so I can't wait to go back and try them out again!

Update: Fries are much better since the first time.</review>

<Text>I saw this place a few times in my yelp, but assumed it was going to be expensive. After seeing photos of the menu, it was actually really affordable. The wings looked really good too. They had a wide variety of sauces and sides. It also has a lot more seating than I thought.

We ordered 20 wings for $20, the house salad, and garlic fries. We tried the dragon, salt and pepper, and cali rub. Everything was overall really good! Of the three, I think dragon was my favorite. It's similar to San Tung wings, but San Tung's is def superior. The salt and pepper and cali rub were pretty standard, but still good! The house salad was only $6, but was a good size to share. The garlic fries were good too; they use thicker cut fries so I liked it. The soda machine was also really fancy.

I would definitely come back again. Bonchon used to be our go-to wing place, but it was getting too expensive. So, I'm really glad we found this new place. I definitely want to try some of their other flavors.< /Text>< rate>

I was extremely happy to see a new wing place in San Mateo. The food seemed good and I thought I would give it a shot. <username>Levon Karagozian< /username><time>1510353772707</time><Rate>5< /Rate>< review>
Prior posts are spot on.  I have been coming to this barber shop for nearly a year now and have never been disappointed with a cut and I have had nearly all these gentlemen trim my crown and beard.

Unfortunately, prior posts are correct about wait times as well. Expect exceptionally long wait times especially during peak hours.  Some times you may luck out and get a seat right when you walk in, but the vast majority of the time expect a wait.

However there is a good reason why you wait, because you are guaranteed a stellar cut.</review>

I always get a great haircut here. I am not sure I have ever left without giving a gracious tip for the quality of the cut. The only reason I don't give five stars is due to the way the line is set-up. There is no organization and it leads to several awkward interactions where people aren't sure who is next. You also need to be prepared to wait. You WILL get a great haircut, but they take their time. I have waited upwards of an hour at times. Please don't let that dissuade you from going; just plan accordingly.<//review>

< Text>
I've been a car enthusiast since I was three years old.  The sales and service experience at a dealership matters to me, which is why my wife and I have purchased our last three 911s from Circle Porsche including a 2010 Turbo, 2015 Turbo S and 2018 GT3. The dealership is about 25 miles from our home and although there is a nearby Porsche dealer less than three miles away, traveling to Long Beach is a no-brainer for us.
At Circle Porsche, it's not just about selling vehicles.  General Manager, Eric Ernst, has a team of car enthusiasts who have a passion for motorsports.   We have always been treated fairly by a staff that has shared our excitement on each 911 purchase.  Also important is the fact that their deals are highly competitive.

Whether configuring a car for himself or for stock, Eric has ordered some truly exceptional cars and SUVs.  So a visit to the dealership to look at the inventory is always a cool experience.  Currently, there is a 911R on the showroom floor and later this year, Circle Porsche will take delivery of their first 911 GT2 RS.

If you're thinking about buying a new or used Porsche, I highly recommend Circle Porsche.  If you're considering a sports car, definitely drive a Porsche.  There are three "Rs" that really matter to me: Racing pedigree, Reputation, and Reliability.  All of these contribute to vehicles that are a blast to drive under all conditions and that represent Porsche's commitment to engineering and high performance.

Finally, Eric Ernst is part of the family that owns other dealerships in the area.  There aren't many family-owned dealerships anymore and a trip to Circle Porsche will make it apparent why the difference between their dealership and others owned by conglomerates is totally in the customer's best interests.

Happy Shopping and Enjoy Your Next Vehicle!<//Text>

< Review>
So stoked! I have been here three times. The first time I was there to see a pre owned 911, but the car sold before I got there. I went back a few weeks later because I saw a very nice low mileage 2012 MBZ E63 Wagon. I was hesitant, because I didn't want to get beat up on my trade ('07 Z06 Corvette). I met with Joe Grimaldi who very graciously let me look the car over (he moved it into the shade and left me and my wife alone) at my leisure.
Joe followed up with me a few days later. He said that the car was still available, and that they hosting a special event on Saturday. I returned, with my trade to drive the E63. after a test drive and some simple and painless negotiation, I was the proud new owner of the E63.
